Therefore Rashi explains, “Devorah and Barak sang.<TIE>.<TIE>.” [and due to Barak, @hh<HEB> הנותן@ee<ENG>is in the masculine form]. @p1@p2Onkelos translates: “His lot will fall”.<TIE>.<TIE>.@p3 Rashi is saying that this is how Onkelos actually translates this verse. According to Onkelos, @hh<HEB>הנותן אמרי שפר@ee<ENG> means that Naftali will give thanks with beautiful words for his lot. But when Rashi wrote above, “‘He delivers pleasant sayings,’ as Onkelos translates it,” it means as follows: The first explanation holds that @hh<HEB>אילה שלוחה@ee<ENG> refers to the fruits of Ginosar, according to which @hh<HEB>אמרי שפר@ee<ENG> means as Onkelos said. [I.e., he will give thanks with beautiful words. But this will be interpreted differently:] the people of Naftali will [give thanks by] reciting the appropriate blessing over the fruits.<QC>
@p1@p222 Many daughters climbed — each one.<TIE>.<TIE>.@p3 Rashi is answering the question: [Why does it say] @hh<HEB>בנות@ee<ENG>, implying there were many, and also say @hh<HEB>צעדה@ee<ENG>, implying there was but one? Thus Rashi explains, “Many daughters climbed — each one.<TIE>.<TIE>.” @p1@p2The letter @HB<HEB>ת@BO<ENG> is added for stylistic purposes.@p3 I.e., it is not the @hh<HEB>ת@ee<ENG> of the feminine form, as it is speaking of a masculine subject. @P1@p2@HB<HEB>פרת@BO<ENG> meaning, being fruitful and multiplying.<TIE>.<TIE>.@p3 Rashi is answering the question: How did Onkelos know that it should be translated so? Thus Rashi explains, “@hh<HEB>פרת@ee<ENG> meaning, being fruitful and multiplying.”<QC>
@p1[23]@p2<TIE>His brothers made him bitter.@p3 [Rashi knows it means his brothers] because at the end of the verse it is written @hh<HEB>בעלי חצים@ee<ENG>, similar to @hh<HEB>ותהי המחצה@ee<ENG> (Bamidbar 31:36), referring to those who are fit to share the inheritance with him, [as Rashi explains]. @p1@p2Potiphar and his wife made him bitter.<TIE>.<TIE>.@p3 [Rashi knows] that it cannot refer to his brothers alone. For then it should say, “They quarreled with him and made him bitter” — as it cannot be that they first embittered his life and then became his antagonists. Perforce, it refers also to Potiphar and his wife.<QC>
@p1[24]@p2<TIE>Because he secretly kept the Torah. This is an addition.<TIE>.<TIE>.@p3 I.e., Onkelos added [an explanation] to the verse. @p1@p2Father and son, @HB<HEB>אבהן ובנין@BO<ENG>.<TIE>.<TIE>.@p3 Rashi is saying that Onkelos translated @hh<HEB>אבן@ee<ENG> as “father and son.” And how did Onkelos know it means this? Therefore Rashi explains that “@hh<HEB>אבן@ee<ENG> is a contraction of @hh<HEB>אב ובן@ee<ENG>.”<QC>
@p1[25]@p2<TIE>So, too, the word @HB<HEB>שדים@BO<ENG> here.<TIE>.<TIE>.@p3 Rashi is explaining how the word @hh<HEB>שדים@ee<ENG> means father. @p1[26]@p2<TIE>@HB<HEB>הריון@BO<ENG> .<TIE>.<TIE>. i.e., “The one who made my mother conceive me”.<TIE>.<TIE>.@p3 Rashi is explaining how the word @hh<HEB>הורי@ee<ENG> means father. @hh<HEB>ויפוזו זרועי ידיו@ee<ENG> as @hh<HEB>ויפוצו@ee<ENG>.<TIE>.<TIE>. Rashi is saying that @hh<HEB>ז@ee<ENG> and @hh<HEB>צ@ee<ENG> often interchange, as in @hh<HEB>זעקת@ee<ENG> which is like @hh<HEB>צעקת@ee<ENG>. @p1@p2@HB<HEB>תאות עולם@BO<ENG> from the same meaning as desire and longing.<TIE>.<TIE>.@p3 Accordingly, @hh<HEB>עד תאות גבעות עולם@ee<ENG> means as follows: the blessings my father gave me were stronger — better — than the blessings Hashem gave my father. This is so, since the great ones [i.e., “the pillars”] of the earth longed for my blessings. And Rashi then explains who longed for them: it was Yaakov’s mother. (@ITsource unknown@it) @p1@p2And @HB<HEB>וגבעות@BO<ENG> .<TIE>.<TIE>. for which his mother longed.<TIE>.<TIE>.@p3 Rashi is answering the question: Onkelos explained @hh<HEB>תאות@ee<ENG> as longing. And before that, it is written @hh<HEB>ברכות אביך גברו וגו'@ee<ENG>, which Rashi previously explained as, “The blessings that Hashem blessed me surpassed the blessings that He blessed my forebears.” If so, according to Onkelos, how does the phrase following @hh<HEB>עד תאות גבעות עולם@ee<ENG> fit in? Therefore Rashi explains, “His mother longed for them.” Rashi is saying that according to Onkelos, @hh<HEB>תאות גבעות עולם@ee<ENG> refers to Rivkah, Yaakov’s mother. She desired those blessings and made Yaakov receive them. Therefore she dressed Yaakov in Eisov’s garments that were desired (@hh<HEB>החמודות@ee<ENG>), in order that Yaakov should receive the blessings.<QC>
@p1[27]@p2<TIE>He is a wolf, for he preys.<TIE>.<TIE>.@p3 [Rashi is saying that] @hh<HEB>יטרף@ee<ENG> does not apply to @hh<HEB>זאב@ee<ENG>, for [this would not need to be stated since] every wolf preys. Rather, @hh<HEB>יטרף@ee<ENG> applies to Binyamin. It is saying that Binyamin is a wolf because he preys like one. But @ITMaharshal@it explains that [Rashi is answering the objection:] The verse seems to say that Binyamin will prey on the wolf. However, “preying” cannot be said about a person. Thus Rashi explains, “He is a wolf, for he preys.”<QC>
@p1[28]@p2<TIE>“And this is what their father spoke to them”.<TIE>.<TIE>. referring to everything that was said above.@p3 [Rashi is saying] that if not for, “And this is what their father spoke to them,” we would think Yaakov altogether regretted what he had said, and took back his reproach. For it says, “He blessed them,” implying they all [received blessings and not reproaches]. Thus Rashi says, “And this is.<TIE>.<TIE>.” to teach that whatever Yaakov had said remained in force, but he then included them all [in the blessings]. (@ITR. Noson@it) @p1@p2 “He blessed them,” which implies all of them.@p3 I did not find this explanation in any Midrash. Furthermore, it seems odd, for where does it state what Yaakov blessed Reuvein, Shimon and Leivi? If it is because he included them all in one blessing, that was learned from @hh<HEB>ברך אותם@ee<ENG> [at the end of the verse]. If so, why is @hh<HEB>ויברך אותם@ee<ENG> necessary?<QC>
@p1[33]@p2<TIE>Our father Yaakov did not die.@p3 The Gemora in Taanis 5b objects, “Did not the doctors embalm Yaakov (Bereishis 50:2)? And does it not say that his sons carried him from Egypt and buried him in Eretz Yisrael (ibid v. 13)? The answer is: It means he did not taste death, i.e., he did not feel the pain of death. Much more has been said on this subject.<QC>
@p1[3]@p2<TIE>They completed the days of his embalming until forty days.@p3 Rashi is answering the question: [Why does it say @hh<HEB>וימלאו@ee<ENG>?] The term @hh<HEB>מלוי@ee<ENG> (completion) applies only to a predetermined number, such as: “I will fill (@hh<HEB>אמלא@ee<ENG>) the number of your days” (Shemos 23:26), meaning the number of days apportioned to you. Similarly (25:24): “When her days of pregnancy were completed (@hh<HEB>וימלאו@ee<ENG>),” meaning the number of days apportioned for her pregnancy. There are many [other examples of this] in Scripture. But here, there was no predetermined number, so Rashi needed to add: “They completed the days @ITof his embalming@it.” Their period for embalming was for a predetermined number of forty days, as Rashi goes on to say. Rashi says @hh<HEB>השלימו@ee<ENG> instead of @hh<HEB>וימלאו@ee<ENG>, to teach that this @hh<HEB>מילוי@ee<ENG> denotes “completion,” rather than denoting “full” which is the opposite of empty. (@ITRe’m@it) @p1@p2Forty days of the embalming period and thirty for mourning.<TIE>.<TIE>.@p3 [Rashi explains] that the seventy days of mourning are not in addition to the forty days mentioned here. @p1@p2Because a blessing had come to them on account of him.<TIE>.<TIE>.@p3 [Rashi knows this] because otherwise, why did they weep? It could not have been to honor Yoseif, because a person cannot weep at will.<QC>
@p1[5]@p2<TIE>Related to @HB<HEB>כרי דגור@BO<ENG>.<TIE>.<TIE>.@p3 @hh<HEB>כרי@ee<ENG> is Hebrew, and @hh<HEB>דגור@ee<ENG> is Aramaic. @p1[6]@p2<TIE>Not to reveal about the Hebrew Language.<TIE>.<TIE>.@p3 Question: If so, how was Yoseif allowed to speak to his brothers in Hebrew? Rashi explained [that Yoseif spoke to them in Hebrew] on, “I speak to you with my own mouth” (45:12). The answer is: Pharaoh stipulated with Yoseif not to speak Hebrew specifically to the Egyptians. When Yoseif spoke to his brothers, no one else was with him in the house, and it did not become known that he spoke to them. (@ITRe’m@it) The @ITNachalas Yaakov@it writes: The real question is that everything Yoseif’s interpreter spoke [to the brothers] was in Hebrew, and many Egyptians were present. Furthermore, @ITRe’m@it contradicts himself, because he wrote on 45:12 that many Egyptians knew Hebrew [since it was the language of the neighboring land of Canaan]. If so, what use was it for Yoseif to swear not to speak in Hebrew, when many Egyptians were speaking it [even though Pharaoh did not understand Hebrew]? See his elaboration there.<QC>
@p1[15]@p2<TIE>Out of respect to his father. But once Yaakov died he no longer received them warmly.@p3 It says in Bereishis Rabbah: “R. Tanchuma said that Yoseif’s intent was for the sake of Heaven, for he reasoned, ‘In the past, my father would seat me above Yehudah who is the king, and above Reuvein who is the firstborn. Now, it is not right for me to sit above them.<TIE>.<TIE>.’” And he did not wish to sit below them, because it would be disrespectful to the royalty [of Egypt]. @p1@p2But there is no other example of this in Scripture.<TIE>.<TIE>.@p3 Rashi is saying: although there is no other example in Scripture, still we can say that @hh<HEB>לו@ee<ENG> means @hh<HEB>שמא@ee<ENG> (lest). This is because @hh<HEB>לו@ee<ENG> sometimes means @hh<HEB>אולי@ee<ENG>, (perhaps), as Rashi proved from Scripture. And @hh<HEB>אולי@ee<ENG> sometimes means @hh<HEB>שמא@ee<ENG>. If so, @hh<HEB>לו@ee<ENG> can mean @hh<HEB>שמא@ee<ENG>, since @hh<HEB>לו@ee<ENG> and @hh<HEB>אולי@ee<ENG> are the same. @p1@p2Sometimes @HB<HEB>אולי@BO<ENG> denotes a wish.<TIE>.<TIE>.@p3 Rashi is saying there is another proof that @hh<HEB>לו@ee<ENG> and @hh<HEB>אולי@ee<ENG> are the same: @hh<HEB>לו@ee<ENG> often means @hh<HEB>בקשה@ee<ENG> (a wish), and @hh<HEB>אולי@ee<ENG> sometimes means @hh<HEB>בקשה@ee<ENG>. Thus we can say that @hh<HEB>לו@ee<ENG> sometimes means @hh<HEB>שמא@ee<ENG> just like @hh<HEB>אולי@ee<ENG> sometimes does. [Rashi adds:] “Sometimes @hh<HEB>אולי@ee<ENG> has the meaning of ‘if’,” [just like @hh<HEB>לו@ee<ENG> does] as Rashi said before. Therefore, @hh<HEB>לו@ee<ENG> and @hh<HEB>אולי@ee<ENG> are the same. @p1[16]@p2<TIE>Who was it that they charged [to be messengers]? The sons of Bilhah.<TIE>.<TIE>.@p3 [Rashi knows this] because the messenger could not have been an individual who was not their brother. For then Yoseif surely would not believe him, as Yoseif knew that his father did not suspect him of this. But now that they sent one of the brothers to him, to stand in front of him and say, “Father charged me with this message,” Yoseif could not deny its truth. [Another reason the messenger could not have been an individual who was not their brother:] It is not logical that they would divulge to a stranger that they sold their brother. This was a secret and was to their disgrace. It would be more fitting to speak to him themselves. (@ITGur Aryeh@it)<QC>
@p1[21]@p2<TIE>Ten lights cannot extinguish one light.<TIE>.<TIE>.@p3 [You might ask: Why did Yoseif compare them to lights? The answer is:] Because the twelve tribes correspond to the twelve stars which illuminate the whole world. Therefore he mentioned to them “ten lights.” I.e., he was saying that despite their plan to kill him, he was saved from them because each tribe is like a constellation in the heavens which cannot be destroyed. And surely he alone is unable to destroy them. But it cannot simply mean that [since ten could not kill him, surely] he cannot kill ten. This would be no proof because Yoseif was a king and could order a thousand people to kill them. (@ITGur Aryeh@it)<QC>
